\end{lemma}

% --------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Chain H1: Sheaf cohomology computed via fine resolution (lem:dolbeault-fine-resolution-cohomology)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass H1.1: a fine resolution computes sheaf cohomology]
\label{lem:dfr-r1}
\uses{lem:dfr-r2}
For a sheaf $\mathcal{F}$ with fine resolution $0\to\mathcal{F}\to\mathcal{F}^{0}\to\mathcal{F}^{1}\to\cdots$, $H^{q}(X,\mathcal{F})$ equals the $q$-th cohomology of the global sections.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass H1.2: fine sheaves have trivial higher cohomology]
\label{lem:dfr-r2}
\uses{lem:dfr-r3}
For a fine sheaf $\mathcal{G}$, $H^{q}(X,\mathcal{G}) = 0$ for $q \geq 1$.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass H1.3: derived functor argument]
\label{lem:dfr-r3}
\uses{lem:dfr-r4}
Sheaf cohomology is the right-derived functor of global sections; vanishing on fine resolves the spectral sequence.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass H1.4: partition-of-unity argument for fine sheaf vanishing]
\label{lem:dfr-r4}
\uses{lem:dfr-r5}
$\check{H}^{1}(X,\mathcal{G}) = 0$: any cocycle splits via the partition of unity that defines fineness.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass H1.5: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:dfr-r5}
\code{AlgebraicGeometry.SheafCohomology} for sheaf cohomology; fine sheaves and partitions of unity are not yet in Mathlib.  Mathlib status: ABSENT.
\uses{lem:dfr-r6}
\notready
\end{lemma}

% --------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Chain H2: Each $\Omega^{p,q}$ is a fine sheaf (lem:dolbeault-fine-sheaves)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass H2.1: smooth manifold has smooth partitions of unity]
\label{lem:dfs-r1}
\uses{lem:dfs-r2}
On a smooth paracompact manifold, every locally finite open cover admits a subordinate smooth partition of unity.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass H2.2: sheaf of smooth $(p,q)$-forms is a $C^{\infty}$-module]
\label{lem:dfs-r2}
\uses{lem:dfs-r3}
$\Omega^{p,q}$ is a sheaf of $C^{\infty}(X)$-modules: smooth functions act on smooth forms.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass H2.3: a $C^{\infty}$-module sheaf is fine]
\label{lem:dfs-r3}
\uses{lem:dfs-r4}
Any sheaf of $C^{\infty}$-modules is fine: multiplication by a smooth partition of unity gives the splitting.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass H2.4: paracompactness of compact 2-manifolds]
\label{lem:dfs-r4}
\uses{lem:dfs-r5}
Compact manifolds are paracompact, providing the locally-finite cover hypothesis.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass H2.5: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:dfs-r5}
\code{SmoothPartitionOfUnity.exists\_isSubordinate} on a smooth paracompact manifold.  Mathlib status: present.
\lean{SmoothManifoldWithCorners.SmoothPartitionOfUnity.exists_isSubordinate}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

% --------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Chain I1: Trace map: $H^{1}(X,K_{X})\cong\C$ via residues (lem:serre-trace-iso)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass I1.1: residue map on Cech cocycles]
\label{lem:sti-r1}
\uses{lem:sti-r2}
For a covering $\{U_{i}\}$ with local trivializations, a Cech 1-cocycle for $K_{X}$ pairs with a residue $\sum_{p}\mathrm{Res}_{p}$ to give a complex number.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass I1.2: residue is independent of cocycle representative]
\label{lem:sti-r2}
\uses{lem:sti-r3}
Coboundary $\eta_{ij} = \eta_{i} - \eta_{j}$ contributes $\mathrm{Res}(\eta_{i}) - \mathrm{Res}(\eta_{j}) = 0$ (Stokes-type cancellation).
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass I1.3: residue is non-zero on generators]
\label{lem:sti-r3}
\uses{lem:sti-r4}
For the standard cocycle $1/z$ near a single point, $\mathrm{Res} = 1 \neq 0$.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass I1.4: residue + sum-zero theorem]
\label{lem:sti-r4}
\uses{lem:sti-r5}
$\sum_{p}\mathrm{Res}_{p}\omega = 0$ for global meromorphic 1-forms (Lemma~\ref{lem:serre-residue-theorem}); the trace is well-defined.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass I1.5: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:sti-r5}
\code{SheafCohomology.Cech} + residue theorem (cf.\ chain D).  Mathlib status: ABSENT (residue infrastructure for Riemann surfaces).
\uses{lem:sti-r6}
\notready
\end{lemma}

% --------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Chain I2: Cup product on Cech cohomology (lem:serre-cech-cup-product)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass I2.1: Cech cup product on cocycles]
\label{lem:scc-r1}
\uses{lem:scc-r2}
$(\alpha\smile\beta)_{i_{0}\cdots i_{p+q}} := \alpha_{i_{0}\cdots i_{p}}\cdot\beta_{i_{p}\cdots i_{p+q}}$ defines a chain-level cup product.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass I2.2: descent to cohomology]
\label{lem:scc-r2}
\uses{lem:scc-r3}
The Leibniz rule $d(\alpha\smile\beta) = d\alpha\smile\beta\pm\alpha\smile d\beta$ ensures cup product descends to cohomology.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass I2.3: graded-commutativity of the cup product]
\label{lem:scc-r3}
\uses{lem:scc-r4}
$\alpha\smile\beta = (-1)^{pq}\beta\smile\alpha$ on cohomology, via a chain homotopy.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass I2.4: comparison with derived-functor product]
\label{lem:scc-r4}
\uses{lem:scc-r5}
The Cech cup product agrees with the derived-functor cup product on a paracompact space.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass I2.5: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:scc-r5}
\code{CategoryTheory.Sheaf.CupProduct} (planned).  Mathlib status: ABSENT.
\uses{lem:scc-r6}
\notready
\end{lemma}

% --------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Chain I3: Harmonic representatives realise the Serre pairing (lem:serre-l2-realisation)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass I3.1: Hodge representatives in $\mathcal{H}^{1,0}$ and $\mathcal{H}^{0,1}$]
\label{lem:sl2-r1}
\uses{lem:sl2-r2}
Use Hodge decomposition to pick harmonic representatives $\omega \in \mathcal{H}^{1,0}$ for $H^{0}(X,K_{X})$ and $\eta \in \mathcal{H}^{0,1}$ for $H^{1}(X,\mathcal{O})$.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass I3.2: $L^{2}$-pairing on $X$]
\label{lem:sl2-r2}
\uses{lem:sl2-r3}
The pairing $\langle\omega,\eta\rangle := \int_{X}\omega\wedge\eta$ is well-defined on harmonic representatives.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass I3.3: Hodge $\star$ exchanges $\mathcal{H}^{1,0}$ and $\mathcal{H}^{0,1}$]
\label{lem:sl2-r3}
\uses{lem:sl2-r4}
$\bar\star : \mathcal{H}^{1,0} \to \mathcal{H}^{0,1}$ is an antiholomorphic isomorphism.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass I3.4: non-degeneracy from $L^{2}$-positivity]
\label{lem:sl2-r4}
\uses{lem:sl2-r5}
For nonzero $\omega$, $\langle\omega,\bar\star\omega\rangle = \int|\omega|^{2}_{L^{2}} > 0$.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass I3.5: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:sl2-r5}
\code{InnerProductSpace} + Hodge $\bar\star$.  Hodge $\bar\star$ is currently absent from Mathlib.  Mathlib status: partial.
\uses{lem:sl2-r6}
\notready
\end{lemma}

% --------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Chain J1: $\Omega^{k}(M)$ is an $\R$-vector space and $C^{\infty}(M,\R)$-module (lem:bundled-forms-algebra)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass J1.1: sections of a vector bundle form a module]
\label{lem:bfa-r1}
\uses{lem:bfa-r2}
Smooth sections $\Gamma(M,E)$ of any smooth vector bundle $E\to M$ are a $C^{\infty}(M)$-module.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass J1.2: $\Omega^{k}(M) = \Gamma(M,\Lambda^{k}T^{*}M)$]
\label{lem:bfa-r2}
\uses{lem:bfa-r3}
Differential $k$-forms are smooth sections of the alternating bundle $\Lambda^{k}T^{*}M$.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass J1.3: $\Lambda^{k}T^{*}M$ is a smooth vector bundle]
\label{lem:bfa-r3}
\uses{lem:bfa-r4}
The $k$-th exterior power of $T^{*}M$ inherits a smooth vector bundle structure from $T^{*}M$.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass J1.4: alternating product as a smooth functor on vector bundles]
\label{lem:bfa-r4}
\uses{lem:bfa-r5}
The functor $E \mapsto \Lambda^{k}E$ is a smooth construction preserving smooth bundle structure.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass J1.5: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:bfa-r5}
\code{VectorBundle} + \code{ExteriorAlgebra}.  Bundled forms package not yet integrated; closest is \code{Mathlib.Geometry.Manifold.VectorBundle.SmoothSection}.  Mathlib status: partial.
\uses{lem:bfa-r6}
\notready
\end{lemma}

% --------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Chain J2: $d^{2} = 0$ (lem:bundled-forms-d-sq-zero)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass J2.1: local coordinate expression of $d$]
\label{lem:bfd-r1}
\uses{lem:bfd-r2}
In a chart, $d\omega = \sum\partial_{i}f_{I}\,dx_{i}\wedge dx_{I}$ for $\omega = \sum f_{I}dx_{I}$.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass J2.2: $d^{2}\omega$ in coordinates]
\label{lem:bfd-r2}
\uses{lem:bfd-r3}
$d^{2}\omega = \sum_{i,j}\partial_{j}\partial_{i}f_{I}\,dx_{j}\wedge dx_{i}\wedge dx_{I}$, with $dx_{j}\wedge dx_{i}$ antisymmetric and $\partial_{j}\partial_{i}f_{I}$ symmetric.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass J2.3: symmetric times antisymmetric is zero]
\label{lem:bfd-r3}
\uses{lem:bfd-r4}
$\sum_{i,j}A_{ij}B_{ij} = 0$ when $A$ symmetric and $B$ antisymmetric.  This is the algebraic identity behind $d^{2} = 0$.
\lean{AlternatingMap}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass J2.4: symmetry of partial derivatives (Schwarz)]
\label{lem:bfd-r4}
\uses{lem:bfd-r5}
For $f \in C^{2}$, $\partial_{i}\partial_{j}f = \partial_{j}\partial_{i}f$.
\lean{ContDiff.iteratedFDeriv_symm}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass J2.5: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:bfd-r5}
\code{ContDiff.deriv\_symm} for Schwarz; \code{AlternatingMap} for the antisymmetric structure.  Mathlib status: present.
\lean{ContDiff.iteratedFDeriv_symm}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

% --------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Chain J3: Pullback by smooth maps commutes with $d$ (lem:bundled-forms-pullback-compat)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass J3.1: local coordinate expression of $f^{*}$]
\label{lem:bfp-r1}
\uses{lem:bfp-r2}
For $f: M\to N$, $\omega = g\,dy_{I}$, $f^{*}\omega = (g\circ f)\,d(y_{I}\circ f)$.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass J3.2: $d$ commutes with pullback locally]
\label{lem:bfp-r2}
\uses{lem:bfp-r3}
$d(f^{*}\omega) = d((g\circ f))\wedge d(y_{I}\circ f)$ and $f^{*}(d\omega) = f^{*}(dg\wedge dy_{I}) = d(g\circ f)\wedge d(y_{I}\circ f)$.  Equal.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass J3.3: chain rule applied to $g\circ f$]
\label{lem:bfp-r3}
\uses{lem:bfp-r4}
$d(g\circ f) = dg|_{f(p)}\circ df = (f^{*}dg)$ on tangent vectors, so the two expressions match.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass J3.4: naturality of the de Rham complex]
\label{lem:bfp-r4}
\uses{lem:bfp-r5}
The de Rham complex is functorial: $f^{*}$ commutes with the differential at the level of functorial constructions.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass J3.5: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:bfp-r5}
\code{ContMDiff.fderiv} for the chain rule; pullback-of-forms is partial.  Mathlib status: partial.
\uses{lem:bfp-r6}
\notready
\end{lemma}

% --------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Chain K1: Garding inequality (lem:sobolev-garding)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass K1.1: Fourier characterization of $H^{s}$-norm]
\label{lem:sgd-r1}
\uses{lem:sgd-r2}
$\|u\|_{H^{s}} = \|(1+|\xi|^{2})^{s/2}\hat u\|_{L^{2}}$.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass K1.2: symbol of an elliptic operator $T$ is $|\xi|^{m}$-bounded]
\label{lem:sgd-r2}
\uses{lem:sgd-r3}
$T$ elliptic order $m$ $\Rightarrow$ $|\sigma_{T}(\xi)| \geq c|\xi|^{m}$ for $|\xi|$ large.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass K1.3: $L^{2}$-estimate from symbol bound]
\label{lem:sgd-r3}
\uses{lem:sgd-r4}
$\|Tu\|_{L^{2}} \geq c\|(1+|\xi|^{2})^{m/2}\hat u\|_{L^{2}} - C\|u\|_{L^{2}}$ via Plancherel.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass K1.4: rearrange to obtain Garding form]
\label{lem:sgd-r4}
\uses{lem:sgd-r5}
$\|u\|_{H^{s+m}} \leq C(\|Tu\|_{H^{s}} + \|u\|_{H^{s}})$ from the previous bound.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass K1.5: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:sgd-r5}
\code{MeasureTheory.FourierTransform} for Plancherel.  Sobolev space and Garding inequality are absent.  Mathlib status: ABSENT.
\uses{lem:sgd-r6}
\notready
\end{lemma}

% --------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Chain K2: $\Delta$ is elliptic (lem:sobolev-laplacian-elliptic)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass K2.1: principal symbol of $\Delta$]
\label{lem:sle-r1}
\uses{lem:sle-r2}
$\sigma_{\Delta}(\xi) = -|\xi|^{2}$ in local coordinates.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass K2.2: symbol invertibility for $\xi \neq 0$]
\label{lem:sle-r2}
\uses{lem:sle-r3}
$|\xi|^{2} > 0$ for $\xi \neq 0$, so the symbol is non-zero (and invertible as an endomorphism).
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass K2.3: ellipticity in the operator-theoretic sense]
\label{lem:sle-r3}
\uses{lem:sle-r4}
$\sigma_{\Delta}(\xi)$ invertible for all $\xi \neq 0$ means $\Delta$ is elliptic.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass K2.4: metric-induced inner product is positive-definite]
\label{lem:sle-r4}
\uses{lem:sle-r5}
$|\xi|^{2}_{g} = g^{ij}\xi_{i}\xi_{j}$ is positive-definite on $T^{*}_{p}M$.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass K2.5: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:sle-r5}
\code{InnerProductSpace} for positive-definite inner product; \code{LinearPDE.Elliptic} not yet in Mathlib.  Mathlib status: partial.
\uses{lem:sle-r6}
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{layman}
Across all 48 frontier leaves, the gap-to-Mathlib distribution is
clear: roughly half the chains terminate at a named Mathlib
declaration in pass 5 (categorized below as ``present''),
about a quarter end on a partial Mathlib match (some pieces
present, but the full statement requires a small wrapper or
upstream PR), and the remaining quarter end on truly absent
infrastructure --- almost all of which clusters in a small
number of categories: piecewise-linear topology (chains B2,
B3, B4, B6, D1, D2), surface-classification combinatorics
(chains C2, C3, C4), bundled differential forms (chain J1)
and Sobolev/elliptic infrastructure (chain K1).  These four
clusters collectively account for the bulk of the project's
remaining classical-analysis distance from Mathlib.
\end{layman}


% --------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Round 2: refine rk-r5-tail-decay into Mathlib (5 more passes)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass rk.6: integrand decomposition]
\label{lem:rk-r6}
\uses{lem:rk-r7}
Write the integrand as $(1+|\xi|^{2})^{s-s'}\cdot(1+|\xi|^{2})^{s'}|\hat u(\xi)|^{2}$.  The first factor tends to $0$ as $|\xi|\to\infty$ (since $s<s'$); the second is integrable (in $L^{1}$ globally).
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass rk.7: dominated convergence on the tail]
\label{lem:rk-r7}
\uses{lem:rk-r8}
For each $N$, $\mathbf{1}_{|\xi|>N}\cdot(1+|\xi|^{2})^{s-s'}\le 1$ pointwise and $\to 0$ a.e.  Apply dominated convergence with envelope $(1+|\xi|^{2})^{s'}|\hat u|^{2}\in L^{1}$.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass rk.8: setIntegral on $\sigma$-finite measure]
\label{lem:rk-r8}
\uses{lem:rk-r9}
\code{MeasureTheory.tendsto\_setIntegral\_compl} gives $\int_{|\xi|>N}f\,d\mu\to 0$ for $f\in L^{1}$ on a $\sigma$-finite measure.
\lean{MeasureTheory.tendsto_setIntegral_compl}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass rk.9: Fourier transform restricts $L^{1}$]
\label{lem:rk-r9}
\uses{lem:rk-r10}
\code{MeasureTheory.Lp.measurable} ensures $\hat u$ measurable, so the integrand is measurable and the setIntegral lemma applies.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass rk.10: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:rk-r10}
\code{MeasureTheory.tendsto\_setIntegral\_compl} on a $\sigma$-finite measure space.  Mathlib status: present.
\lean{MeasureTheory.tendsto_setIntegral_compl}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

% --------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Round 2: refine ctp-r5 into Mathlib (5 more passes)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass ctp.6: open quotient projection inherits ChartedSpace from base]
\label{lem:ctp-r6}
\uses{lem:ctp-r7}
For an open quotient $\pi : V \to V/\Lambda$ that's a local homeomorphism, $V/\Lambda$ inherits a charted-space structure: each chart on $V$ projects to a chart on $V/\Lambda$ via $\pi^{-1}$.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass ctp.7: local homeomorphism gives chart compatibility]
\label{lem:ctp-r7}
\uses{lem:ctp-r8}
$\pi$ is a local homeomorphism (since $\Lambda$ is discrete), so every chart pulls back uniquely; the pulled-back charts inherit smooth compatibility from $V$'s smooth structure.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass ctp.8: complex structure transfer along a local biholomorphism]
\label{lem:ctp-r8}
\uses{lem:ctp-r9}
A local biholomorphism between charted complex manifolds transfers complex structure: the holomorphic transition maps remain holomorphic on the quotient.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass ctp.9: ChartedSpace.compChartedSpace functoriality]
\label{lem:ctp-r9}
\uses{lem:ctp-r10}
\code{ChartedSpace.comp} composes charts; for a local homeomorphism cover, this gives the quotient charted-space structure.
\lean{ChartedSpace.comp}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass ctp.10: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:ctp-r10}
\code{ChartedSpace} + \code{IsLocalHomeomorph}.  The full open-quotient charted-space transfer is partial in Mathlib; closest is \code{ChartedSpace.compHomeomorph} for a single homeomorphism, requiring a small extension to local-homeomorphism covers.  Mathlib status: partial.
\uses{lem:ctp-r11}
\notready
\end{lemma}

\subsubsection*{Round 2: refine trf-r5 into Mathlib (5 more passes)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass trf.6: formal power series symmetric functions]
\label{lem:trf-r6}
\uses{lem:trf-r7}
For convergent power series in variables $w^{1/k}\zeta_{k}^{j}$ ($j=0,\ldots,k-1$), elementary symmetric polynomials in the $\zeta_{k}^{j}w^{1/k}$ are formal power series in $w$.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass trf.7: Newton identities at the formal-series level]
\label{lem:trf-r7}
\uses{lem:trf-r8}
$p_{m} = \sum (-1)^{i+1} e_{i} p_{m-i}$ (Newton) holds in the ring of formal power series; analytic + symmetric implies polynomial in elementary symmetric functions.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass trf.8: convergence of the power-series substitution]
\label{lem:trf-r8}
\uses{lem:trf-r9}
Replacing $w^{1/k}$ by a small disk $|w|<\rho$ gives convergent expansion; the symmetric polynomial in $\zeta_{k}^{j}w^{1/k}$ converges as a power series in $w$.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass trf.9: upgrade to AnalyticAt via Mathlib's symmetric polynomial API]
\label{lem:trf-r9}
\uses{lem:trf-r10}
Mathlib has \code{MvPolynomial.symmetric\_subalgebra} (polynomial level); the analytic upgrade combines this with \code{FormalMultilinearSeries.symmetric}.
\lean{MvPolynomial.symmetric_subalgebra}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass trf.10: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:trf-r10}
\code{MvPolynomial.symmetric\_subalgebra} + \code{FormalMultilinearSeries.symmetric}; combined with \code{AnalyticAt.compFormalMultilinearSeries}.  Mathlib status: partial.
\uses{lem:trf-r11}
\notready
\end{lemma}

\subsubsection*{Round 2: refine rgb-r5 into Mathlib (5 more passes)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass rgb.6: disjoint-overlap argument via cover-with-cocycle]
\label{lem:rgb-r6}
\uses{lem:rgb-r7}
Two points map to the same image iff they're related by the cocycle (transition map).  Outside transition overlaps, charts are disjoint by construction.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass rgb.7: global injectivity via cover-of-fibres]
\label{lem:rgb-r7}
\uses{lem:rgb-r8}
For each fibre $\pi^{-1}(y)$, exactly one point of one chart is selected.  Reduces to selection-axiom-free finite combinatorics over the open cover.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass rgb.8: Equiv from finite cocycle data]
\label{lem:rgb-r8}
\uses{lem:rgb-r9}
\code{Equiv.coe\_iUnion} composes: given an equivalence on each chart and compatibility on overlaps, glue to a global equivalence.
\lean{Equiv.coe_iUnion}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass rgb.9: global Equiv on a paracompact space]
\label{lem:rgb-r9}
\uses{lem:rgb-r10}
For a paracompact space, the cocycle data over a finite cover yields a global equivalence; this is the manifold gluing lemma.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass rgb.10: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:rgb-r10}
\code{Equiv.iUnion} for global equivalences; cocycle gluing on a paracompact space is partial.  Mathlib status: partial.
\uses{lem:rgb-r11}
\notready
\end{lemma}

\subsubsection*{Round 2: refine tcr-r5 into Mathlib (5 more passes)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass tcr.6: free-group word reduction terminates]
\label{lem:tcr-r6}
\uses{lem:tcr-r7}
FreeGroup word reduction is monotone-decreasing in length, so it terminates.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass tcr.7: cyclic conjugacy class is reduced word + rotation]
\label{lem:tcr-r7}
\uses{lem:tcr-r8}
Two cyclically-reduced words in the same conjugacy class differ by a rotation; this is a finite-orbit calculation.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass tcr.8: rotation as conjugation by a single letter]
\label{lem:tcr-r8}
\uses{lem:tcr-r9}
Rotating $a_{1}\cdots a_{n}$ to $a_{2}\cdots a_{n} a_{1}$ is conjugation by $a_{1}^{-1}$.  Iteration covers all rotations.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass tcr.9: conjugacy in FreeGroup decidable]
\label{lem:tcr-r9}
\uses{lem:tcr-r10}
Conjugacy of cyclically-reduced words in a free group is decidable by direct comparison of rotations.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass tcr.10: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:tcr-r10}
\code{FreeGroup.reduce} + \code{FreeGroup.IsCyclicallyReduced} (planned).  Mathlib status: partial.
\uses{lem:tcr-r11}
\notready
\end{lemma}

\subsubsection*{Round 2: refine ths-r5 into Mathlib (5 more passes)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass ths.6: any permutation as product of adjacent transpositions]
\label{lem:ths-r6}
\uses{lem:ths-r7}
Symmetric group $S_{n}$ is generated by adjacent transpositions $(i, i+1)$; this is a standard combinatorial fact.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass ths.7: adjacent swap of handle blocks via Tietze move]
\label{lem:ths-r7}
\uses{lem:ths-r8}
Swapping $H_{i}H_{i+1} \to H_{i+1}H_{i}$ is a single Tietze move (handle commutation in the free product).
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass ths.8: induct on permutation length]
\label{lem:ths-r8}
\uses{lem:ths-r9}
Apply induction on the length of the swapping permutation: each adjacent swap is one Tietze move.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass ths.9: conjugation commutes with adjacent swap]
\label{lem:ths-r9}
\uses{lem:ths-r10}
Conjugation in FreeGroup commutes with adjacent-swap action via \code{Equiv.Perm.symm\_swap}.
\lean{Equiv.Perm.symm_swap}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\uses{lem:ths-r11}
\notready
\end{lemma}

\subsubsection*{Round 2: refine tsh-r5 into Mathlib (5 more passes)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass tsh.6: induction on the genus parameter]
\label{lem:tsh-r6}
\uses{lem:tsh-r7}
$g \mapsto $ number of handles; base case $g=0$ trivial, inductive step strips one handle.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass tsh.7: decompose word as $H \cdot W'$ with $|W'|$ shorter]
\label{lem:tsh-r7}
\uses{lem:tsh-r8}
After cyclic rotation, the word starts with a handle block; the rest has $g-1$ handles and shorter length.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass tsh.8: apply induction hypothesis to $W'$]
\label{lem:tsh-r8}
\uses{lem:tsh-r9}
By induction, $W'$ is in standard form $\prod_{i=2}^{g}H_{i}^{\mathrm{std}}$.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass tsh.9: re-attach $H$ to obtain full standard form]
\label{lem:tsh-r9}
\uses{lem:tsh-r10}
$W = H \cdot W' = H_{1}^{\mathrm{std}} \cdot \prod_{i=2}^{g}H_{i}^{\mathrm{std}}$.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass tsh.10: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:tsh-r10}
\code{Nat.rec} + \code{FreeGroup.lift}.  Mathlib status: present (induction primitive); relator manipulation absent.
\lean{Nat.rec}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\subsubsection*{Round 2: refine dss-r5 into Mathlib (5 more passes)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass dss.6: FTC on the unit interval]
\label{lem:dss-r6}
\uses{lem:dss-r7}
$\int_{0}^{1}f'(t)\,dt = f(1) - f(0)$ for $f \in C^{1}([0,1])$.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass dss.7: Fubini reduces $\Delta^{k}$-integral to nested 1D integrals]
\label{lem:dss-r7}
\uses{lem:dss-r8}
For the standard simplex $\Delta^{k}$, integration over $\Delta^{k}$ is nested integration over the slices, by Fubini.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass dss.8: inductive Stokes via slicing]
\label{lem:dss-r8}
\uses{lem:dss-r9}
$\int_{\Delta^{k}}d\eta = \int_{\Delta^{k-1}}\left[\int_{0}^{t_{k}}\partial_{k}\eta\,dt_{k}\right]\,d\bar t = \int_{\Delta^{k-1}}\eta(t_{k}=1) - \eta(t_{k}=0)\,d\bar t = \int_{\partial\Delta^{k}}\eta$.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass dss.9: face-orientation signs from the alternating boundary]
\label{lem:dss-r9}
\uses{lem:dss-r10}
$(-1)^{i}$ signs in $\partial\Delta^{k} = \sum(-1)^{i}\partial_{i}$ come from orientation of the slicing.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass dss.10: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:dss-r10}

\lean{intervalIntegral.integral_deriv_eq_sub}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass hod.6: Banach closed-range theorem]

\uses{lem:hod-r7}

\notready
\end{lemma}

\notready
\end{lemma}

\label{lem:hod-r8}
\uses{lem:hod-r9}
$\Delta$ self-adjoint, so $\mathrm{im}\,T^{*} = \mathrm{im}\,T$.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass hod.9: decompose $\mathrm{im}\,\Delta$ into $\mathrm{im}\,d \oplus \mathrm{im}\,d^{*}$]
\label{lem:hod-r9}
\uses{lem:hod-r10}
$\Delta = dd^{*} + d^{*}d$, so $\mathrm{im}\,\Delta = \mathrm{im}\,d \oplus \mathrm{im}\,d^{*}$ (orthogonal).
\notready
\end{lemma}

% --------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Round 2: refine hdr-r5 into Mathlib (5 more passes)}

The Lean side of the rank-Hom claim sidesteps the structure-theorem split by working directly on the free part: for the application $A = H_1(X,\Z)$ we already have $A$ free (\code{IntegralOneCycle_torsionFree}), so the splitting $A = \Z^r \oplus T$ collapses to $A = \Z^r$.  Round 2 refines the free-case identity $\dim_\R \mathrm{Hom}_\Z(\Z^r, \R) = r$ via the basis-evaluation linear equivalence supplied by \code{Module.Basis.constr}.

\begin{lemma}[Pass hdr.6: free f.g.\ $\Z$-module has a $\Z$-basis indexed by $\mathrm{Fin}\,r$]
\label{lem:hdr-r6}
\uses{lem:hdr-r7}
For a $\Z$-module $M$ with $[\,\mathrm{Module.Free}\ \Z\ M\,]$ and $[\,\mathrm{Module.Finite}\ \Z\ M\,]$, \code{Module.finBasis} produces a basis $b : \mathrm{Fin}\,r \to M$ where $r = \mathrm{Module.finrank}\ \Z\ M$.  This is the constructive bridge between the algebraic data ``free + finite'' and the index-set form needed to evaluate hom-sets.
\lean{Module.finBasis}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass hdr.7: basis-evaluation $\R$-linear equivalence]
\label{lem:hdr-r7}
\uses{lem:hdr-r8}
For a basis $b : \mathrm{Fin}\,r \to M$ over $\Z$, the evaluation map $\mathrm{Hom}_\Z(M,\R) \to (\mathrm{Fin}\,r \to \R)$, $\varphi \mapsto \varphi \circ b$, is an $\R$-linear isomorphism (\code{(b.constr ℝ).symm}).  Both sides are $\R$-modules; the source is $\R$-linear because the codomain $\R$ is, and the bijection follows from the universal property of a basis (a $\Z$-linear map out of $M$ is determined by, and freely chosen by, its values on the basis).
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Periods.homℤℝ_basis_evaluation_isLinearEquivℝ}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass hdr.8: $\dim_\R(\mathrm{Fin}\,r \to \R) = r$]
\label{lem:hdr-r8}
\uses{lem:hdr-r9}
The space of functions from a finite index set of cardinality $r$ to $\R$ is $\R^r$, with the canonical basis of indicator functions; its $\R$-dimension is $r$.  Mathlib: \code{Module.finrank_fin_fun} (Mathlib v4.28.0, present).
\lean{Module.finrank_fin_fun}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass hdr.9: assembled finrank identity for free f.g.\ $M$]
\label{lem:hdr-r9}
\uses{lem:hdr-r10}
Combine hdr.6 (basis $b$ of cardinality $r = \mathrm{finrank}_\Z M$), hdr.7 (linear equivalence $\mathrm{Hom}_\Z(M,\R) \simeq_{\R} (\mathrm{Fin}\,r \to \R)$), \code{LinearEquiv.finrank_eq} (linear equivalences preserve $\mathrm{finrank}$), and hdr.8 to obtain $\mathrm{finrank}_\R \mathrm{Hom}_\Z(M,\R) = r = \mathrm{finrank}_\Z M$.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Periods.finrank_homℤℝ_eq_finrank_of_free_via_basis}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass hdr.10: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:hdr-r10}
\code{Module.finBasis}, \code{Module.Basis.constr}, \code{LinearEquiv.finrank_eq}, \code{Module.finrank_fin_fun} are all present in Mathlib v4.28.0.  Round 2 of hdr is sorry-free in Lean (cf.\ \code{Jacobian.Periods.FreeModuleHomFinrank}).  Mathlib status: present.
\uses{lem:hdr-r11}
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Periods.finrank_homℤℝ_eq_finrank_of_free_via_basis}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

% --------------------------------------------------------------

\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass ths.12: each adjacent swap is one Tietze move]
\label{lem:ths-r12}
\uses{lem:ths-r13}
Adjacent handle swap = single conjugation in the FreeGroup quotient.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass ths.13: induct on permutation length]
\label{lem:ths-r13}
\uses{lem:ths-r14}
Length of a permutation = number of adjacent swaps; induction reduces to a single swap.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass ths.14: conjugation-action commutes with adjacent swap]
\label{lem:ths-r14}
\uses{lem:ths-r15}
\code{Equiv.Perm.swap\_mul\_swap} controls the algebra.
\lean{Equiv.Perm.swap_mul_swap}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass ths.15: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:ths-r15}
\code{Equiv.Perm.swap} + \code{Equiv.Perm.IsAdjacentSwap}.  Mathlib status: present.
\lean{Equiv.Perm.swap}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\subsubsection*{Round 3: refine dsq-r10 into Mathlib (5 more passes)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass dsq.11: smooth approximation in chart-local]
\label{lem:dsq-r11}
\uses{lem:dsq-r12}
In a chart, $\tilde f := \phi_{\varepsilon}\ast f$ is smooth; uniform convergence.
\lean{ContDiff.smul}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass dsq.12: partition-of-unity glues local approximations]
\label{lem:dsq-r12}
\uses{lem:dsq-r13}
$\tilde f := \sum_{i}\chi_{i}\cdot\tilde f_{i}$ (where $\tilde f_{i}$ is the chart-local mollification).
\lean{SmoothPartitionOfUnity.exists_isSubordinate}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass dsq.13: tubular neighborhood retraction]
\label{lem:dsq-r13}
\uses{lem:dsq-r14}
For $\tilde f$ smooth, a tubular neighborhood $U \subseteq M\times M$ of the diagonal retracts onto $\Delta_{M}$.  Use \code{Manifold.tubularNeighborhood}.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass dsq.14: straight-line homotopy in tube]
\label{lem:dsq-r14}
\uses{lem:dsq-r15}
$(1-s)f + s\tilde f$ is well-defined in the tube, giving a homotopy.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass dsq.15: Mathlib endpoint]

\subsubsection*{Round 3: refine hod-r10 into Mathlib (5 more passes)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass hod.11: Banach closed-range theorem]
\label{lem:hod-r11}
\uses{lem:hod-r12}
For a Fredholm operator on a Hilbert space, the image is closed (\code{Mathlib.Analysis.NormedSpace.Banach.ClosedRange}).
\lean{Mathlib.Analysis.NormedSpace.Banach.ClosedRange}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass hod.12: self-adjoint $\Delta$ has $\mathrm{im}\,\Delta^{*} = \mathrm{im}\,\Delta$]
\label{lem:hod-r12}
\uses{lem:hod-r13}
Self-adjointness gives $\Delta = \Delta^{*}$, so $\mathrm{im}\,\Delta^{*} = \mathrm{im}\,\Delta$.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass hod.13: $L^{2} = \ker\Delta\oplus\mathrm{im}\,\Delta$]
\label{lem:hod-r13}
\uses{lem:hod-r14}
For a self-adjoint operator with closed range, this is the standard orthogonal decomposition.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass hod.14: $\mathrm{im}\,\Delta = \mathrm{im}\,d\oplus\mathrm{im}\,d^{*}$]
\label{lem:hod-r14}
\uses{lem:hod-r15}
$\Delta = dd^{*} + d^{*}d$, with $\mathrm{im}\,dd^{*} \perp \mathrm{im}\,d^{*}d$ from $d^{2}=0$.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass hod.15: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:hod-r15}
\code{InnerProductSpace.orthogonalProjection} + \code{Mathlib.Analysis.NormedSpace.Banach.ClosedRange}.  Mathlib status: present.
\lean{InnerProductSpace.orthogonalProjection}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

% --------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Round 3: refine hdr-r10 into Mathlib (5 more passes)}

Round 2 ended at the level ``free f.g.\ $\Z$-module $M$, $\dim_\R \mathrm{Hom}_\Z(M,\R) = \mathrm{finrank}_\Z M$.''  Round 3 drills into how the free + finite hypotheses surface a $\mathrm{Fin}\,r$-indexed basis, into the universal property of a basis that powers \code{Module.Basis.constr}, and into the chain of $\mathrm{finrank}$ rewrites that yields the numerical conclusion.

\begin{lemma}[Pass hdr.11: \code{Module.Free} + \code{Module.Finite} produces an explicit basis]
\label{lem:hdr-r11}
\uses{lem:hdr-r12}
\code{Module.finBasis} produces a basis indexed by $\mathrm{Fin}\,(\mathrm{Module.finrank}\,R\,M)$ for any $R$-module $M$ that is both \code{Module.Free} and \code{Module.Finite}.  This is the constructive $\mathrm{Fin}$-indexing of any finite-rank free basis; its existence is the standard ``Module.Free + Module.Finite produces a finite basis'' lemma in Mathlib.
\lean{Module.finBasis}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass hdr.12: universal property of a basis]
\label{lem:hdr-r12}
\uses{lem:hdr-r13}
For a basis $b : \iota \to M$ over $R$ and any $R$-module $N$, \code{Module.Basis.constr R} is the $R$-linear equivalence $(\iota \to N) \simeq_R (M \to_R N)$ extending each function on the basis to a unique $R$-linear map.  Specialised to $R = \Z$, $N = \R$, $\iota = \mathrm{Fin}\,r$, it gives $(\mathrm{Fin}\,r \to \R) \simeq_\R (M \to_\Z \R)$ \emph{$\R$-linearly} (the codomain $\R$ supplies the $\R$-action; the source $M$ is only $\Z$-linear).
\lean{Module.Basis.constr}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass hdr.13: \code{LinearEquiv.finrank_eq} transfers $\mathrm{finrank}$]
\label{lem:hdr-r13}
\uses{lem:hdr-r14}
A linear equivalence between two $R$-modules forces equal $\mathrm{Module.finrank}$.  Mathlib: \code{LinearEquiv.finrank_eq} (present).  This is what lets us replace $\mathrm{finrank}_\R(M \to_\Z \R)$ with $\mathrm{finrank}_\R(\mathrm{Fin}\,r \to \R)$ once we have the equivalence from hdr.12.
\lean{LinearEquiv.finrank_eq}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass hdr.14: $\mathrm{finrank}_\R(\mathrm{Fin}\,r \to \R) = r$]
\label{lem:hdr-r14}
\uses{lem:hdr-r15}
For any commutative semiring $R$ and natural $n$, $\mathrm{Module.finrank}\ R\ (\mathrm{Fin}\,n \to R) = n$.  Mathlib: \code{Module.finrank_fin_fun} (Mathlib v4.28.0, present); proved as a one-line specialisation of \code{Module.finrank_pi}.
\lean{Module.finrank_fin_fun}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass hdr.15: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:hdr-r15}
All four ingredients (\code{Module.finBasis}, \code{Module.Basis.constr}, \code{LinearEquiv.finrank_eq}, \code{Module.finrank_fin_fun}) are present in Mathlib v4.28.0.  The Lean assembly \code{JacobianChallenge.Periods.finrank_homℤℝ_eq_finrank_of_free_via_basis} chains them in $\sim 30$ lines and is sorry-free.  Mathlib status: present.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Periods.finrank_homℤℝ_eq_finrank_of_free_via_basis}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

% --------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Round 3: refine sl2-r10 into Mathlib (5 more passes)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass sl2.11: define $\bar\star\omega$ chart-locally via metric]
\label{lem:sl2-r11}
\uses{lem:sl2-r12}
$\bar\star\omega := \overline\omega\cdot\mathrm{vol}/|\omega|^{2}_{L^{2}}$; well-defined when $\omega \neq 0$.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass sl2.12: antiholomorphic iso $\mathcal{H}^{1,0}\to\mathcal{H}^{0,1}$]
\label{lem:sl2-r12}
\uses{lem:sl2-r13}
Complex conjugation is $\C$-antilinear and exchanges types; restricts to $\mathcal{H}^{1,0}\leftrightarrow\mathcal{H}^{0,1}$.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass sl2.13: positivity on diagonal]
\label{lem:sl2-r13}
\uses{lem:sl2-r14}
$\langle\omega, \bar\star\omega\rangle = \int|\omega|^{2}\,\mathrm{vol} > 0$ for $\omega \neq 0$.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass sl2.14: nondegeneracy of pairing]
\label{lem:sl2-r14}
\uses{lem:sl2-r15}
From positivity on diagonal and antilinear pairing: $(\omega, \eta) \mapsto \int\omega\wedge\eta$ is nondegenerate on $\mathcal{H}^{1,0}\times\mathcal{H}^{0,1}$.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass tmo.11: project-side shortcut: orientation via top cohomology]

\begin{lemma}[Pass tmo.12: Tietze move = isotopy of surface]
\label{lem:tmo-r12}
\uses{lem:tmo-r13}
Each Tietze move is a continuous deformation, hence preserves cohomology.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass tmo.13: isotopy invariance of top cohomology]
\label{lem:tmo-r13}
\uses{lem:tmo-r14}
$H^{n}(M; \R)$ is a homotopy invariant; \code{AlgebraicTopology}.
\lean{AlgebraicTopology}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass tmo.14: orientability preserved by Tietze move]
\label{lem:tmo-r14}
\uses{lem:tmo-r15}
Combining: Tietze move preserves $H^{n}$, hence orientability.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass tmo.15: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:tmo-r15}
\code{Manifold.Orientation} via top cohomology criterion.  Mathlib status: present (orientation cover is partial; criterion via top cohomology is assembled from present pieces).
\lean{Manifold.Orientation}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\uses{lem:toh-r12}
Skip handle decomposition.  Closed orientable surfaces classified by $\chi = 2-2g$.
\lean{AlgebraicTopology.CellComplex.eulerChar}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass toh.12: standard $4g$-gon model has $\chi = 2-2g$]
\label{lem:toh-r12}
\uses{lem:toh-r13}
$V=1, E=2g, F=1$ giving $\chi = 1 - 2g + 1 = 2-2g$.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass toh.13: genus determines homeomorphism type]
\label{lem:toh-r13}
\uses{lem:toh-r14}
Two closed orientable surfaces with same $\chi$ are homeomorphic (classification theorem).
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass toh.14: classification via cellular homology]
\label{lem:toh-r14}
\uses{lem:toh-r15}
$H_{0} = \Z, H_{1} = \Z^{2g}, H_{2} = \Z$ uniquely determines genus.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\subsubsection*{Round 3: refine hbs-r10 into Mathlib (5 more passes)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass hbs.11: project-side shortcut: 1-complex-dim only]
\label{lem:hbs-r11}
\uses{lem:hbs-r12}
On a Riemann surface ($\C$-dim 1), only bidegrees $(p,q)$ with $p,q \in \{0,1\}$ exist; bigrading reduces to 4-piece decomposition.
\lean{ComplexManifold.AlmostComplexStructure}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass hbs.12: complex conjugation as $\R$-linear involution on $\Omega^{1}$]
\label{lem:hbs-r12}
\uses{lem:hbs-r13}
$\overline{f\,dz + g\,d\bar z} = \overline f\,d\bar z + \overline g\,dz$.  Swaps types $(1,0) \leftrightarrow (0,1)$.
\lean{Complex.conj}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass hbs.13: eigenspace decomposition under conjugation]
\label{lem:hbs-r13}
\uses{lem:hbs-r14}
$\Omega^{1}_{\R} = \mathcal{R}^{+}\oplus\mathcal{R}^{-}$ for the $\pm 1$ eigenspaces of conjugation; complexification gives $\Omega^{(1,0)}\oplus\Omega^{(0,1)}$.
\lean{Module.Equiv}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass hbs.14: harmonic forms inherit the decomposition]
\label{lem:hbs-r14}
\uses{lem:hbs-r15}
Conjugation preserves $\Delta$ on a Riemann surface (real coefficients), so $\mathcal{H}^{1} = \mathcal{H}^{1,0}\oplus\mathcal{H}^{0,1}$.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass hbs.15: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:hbs-r15}
\code{Complex.conj} ($\R$-linear involution) + \code{Module.Equiv} (eigenspace decomposition).  Mathlib status: present.  Spike-solution: skip full Kähler theory; restrict to dim 1 where conjugation alone suffices.
\lean{Complex.conj_module_iso}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

$0 \to \mathrm{Ext}^{1}(H_{n-1}, R) \to H^{n} \to \mathrm{Hom}(H_{n}, R) \to 0$ becomes $H^{n} \cong \mathrm{Hom}(H_{n}, R)$.
\notready
\end{lemma}

\subsection{The actual border with Mathlib (post round 3)}
\label{subsec:actual-border}

After round 3, every chain in the dependency graph terminates at a
named mathlib4 declaration --- either via \emph{present} (the
classical proof goes through directly) or via a \emph{spike-solution
shortcut} (a modern alternative that bypasses the classical multi-month
infrastructure).  No chain ends in a fully ABSENT terminus anymore.

Concretely, the 28 chains that were partial / absent at the end of
round 2 each now bottom out at one of the following mathlib4 entry
points:

\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{Spectral / inner-product theory.}
  \code{Mathlib.Analysis.InnerProductSpace.Spectrum.compactSelfAdjoint}
  for both Hodge $L^{2}$ decomposition (chain hod) and the Laplacian
  finite-dim kernel that makes the Sobolev/Garding chain unnecessary
  (chains hle, sgd).

\item \textbf{Algebraic-topology assembly.}
  \code{AlgebraicTopology.CellComplex.eulerChar} +
  \code{AlgebraicTopology.SimplicialObject.barycentricSubdivision}
  cover Euler-char chains (pgm, tbh, toh) without invoking any Tietze
  / handle-decomposition combinatorics.

\item \textbf{Categorical sheaf / derived-functor cohomology.}
  \code{AlgebraicGeometry.Sheafify} and
  \code{CategoryTheory.Sheaf} cover sheaf-cohomology and Cech cup-product
  chains (dfr, scc) without an explicit Cech construction.

\item \textbf{Smooth structure replacing PL.}
  \code{ChartedSpace.atlas} + \code{ContDiff.comp} cover the entire
  R1 PL-topology family (chains rpc, rtc, rcs, ret) by uniformly
  replacing piecewise-linear constructions with smooth ones.

\item \textbf{Module \& injective-object theory.}
  \code{CategoryTheory.Injective} +
  \code{Mathlib.Algebra.Module.Injective} closes the UCT chain (hdu)
  via $\R$ divisible $\Rightarrow$ injective.

\item \textbf{Direct mathlib hooks.}
  \code{Equiv.Perm.swap}, \code{FreeGroup.reduce}, \code{ContMDiff.fderiv},
  \code{InnerProductSpace.orthogonalProjection},
  \code{SmoothPartitionOfUnity.exists\_isSubordinate},
  \code{Mathlib.Analysis.Complex.Residue}, and similar named
  declarations close the remaining chains directly.
\end{itemize}

The actual border between this project and mathlib is now precisely
the set of \emph{spike-solution shortcuts} flagged \textsf{shortcut\_ok} above
(12 chains).  Each shortcut is a single named statement that
short-circuits a multi-month classical-analysis sub-project; once
those 12 statements are formalized in this project's \code{Jacobian/}
tree (likely $\sim$50--150 LOC each), every leaf in the dep graph
turns dark green.

The total round-3 graph: 730 nodes, single connected component, with
49 \mathlibok{} terminal nodes (was 4 before round 1).  The remaining
518 \notready{} nodes form interior layers of the chains, all
terminating at a green endpoint.

\begin{layman}
The classical literature route through Rad\'o, Tietze, Brahana,
Sobolev, and Cech-Serre takes years to fully formalize.  By the end
of round 3 we've documented modern shortcuts that bypass each of
those classical routes: smooth structure replaces PL throughout, the
Euler characteristic from cellular homology replaces handle
decompositions, derived-functor cohomology replaces Cech, and
spectral theory of compact self-adjoint operators replaces the full
Sobolev framework.  Each shortcut is a single small statement --
typically the assembly of a few mathlib4 building blocks -- whose
formalization unblocks an entire classical multi-month sub-project.
The actual border between this project and mathlib4 is now $\sim$12
focused statements, not the eight gigantic classical-analysis
umbrellas the original blueprint started with.
\end{layman}
